He has now reached a point where he was willing to give an electric razor another try. The directions appear to be somewhat overwhelming for a senior citizen, what with the sterilization of the razor head and how to clean it vs. an older or cheaper model that you just plug in and shave with.  But he has found that this razor holds its charge and once he has tried it a time or two has found it to be pretty easy  to shave with. The razor heads give him a close clean shave and he enjoys the portability of it. He can now take it with when we travel vs making sure he has shave cream and his razor packed. And the cleaning of the razor head has proven to be pretty simple and it thus sanitizes the razor head assuring him that the next time he uses this electric razor it will be clean and sanitized for him.</li>

    <li> This is an upgrade from my husbands previous Braun razor which he wore out after many years of use.  Since it was a present I had to read a lot of reviews to figure out which one to get.  I wasn&#x27;t crazy about the cleaning system just because it means monthly expenses of the cleaning fluid, but it seems the better razors all have them.  One thing I have since noticed is that the razor gives you the choice of doing the cleaning or not.  Just setting the razor in the unit doesn&#x27;t start it up.  The indicator light lets you know how dirty the razor is and then you have to push the button to activate it.  He&#x27;s only used it for 2 weeks so I don&#x27;t know how long the cleaning fluid really does last.  This is one of the quietest razors I have ever heard though.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve always used Braun shavers and this one is the best yet! Gives a really close shave and has nice features. Well worth the price. You won&#x27;t be disappointed.</li>
    <li> The Braun Series 7-760 cc works very well for me. I upgraded from a $39 Norelco rotary razor and can see the difference. The series 7 defintely gives a much, much smoother shave for the same amount of time. With the series-7, I can feel my chin as smooth as they make out to be in the ads. The motor is pretty powerful and you can feel it revving; the flat but longer cutter does a better job than the rotary blades (for me). I do need to watch myself in a shaving mirror up-close to weed out all the areas neat and clean. The personalization adjustments - where you can increase or decrease the intensity of the razor - works fine on the sensitive areas of the neck. So far, I haven&#x27;t had any red areas after the shave. I do have to stretch my skin as recommended. The cleaning system is a bit of a drain as I look at it. The cleaning cartridge can last upto 60 days, but you will need to replace it - an on-going expense. You can wash the razor under water and the cleaning indicator still says the razor requires the minimum level of cleaning. I plan not to replace the cartridge and stick to water cleaning, though I have to forgo the nice fresh  lemon smell when I have it up-close for shaving. The razor can run off the electric cord straight which is a big plus for me as I personally don&#x27;t like rechargeable batteries - they are not good for the environment. The corded operation means I have less to carry when I travel. While the one sixty bucks price tag is a bit overboard for me for a razor, my shave with the series-7 definitely leaves me satisfied each and every day.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used an electric shaver for all of my adult life and was desperately in need of a replacement. I previously had a Remington which admittedly was a low-end model but it had dual foils and cut extremely close to the skin! Didn&#x27;t need to follow up with a straight razor after shaves. So after reading all of the great reviews for the 7 series decided I needed to upgrade and was willing to pay top dollar for Braun&#x27;s top-of-the-line electric shaver. After 2-3 shaves I was very disappointed in the product. It did not shave as close as my previous low-end $30 Remington and each time I had to follow-up with a straight razor to get it down to the skin. I will say that it does cut very well with few passes, just not down to the skin which is what I was used to. I even tried stretching my skin making several passes but in the end it did not achieve the results I expected. For the price I think it should match if not surpass a $30 electric razor.</li>
    <li> First off, electric shaving experiences can differ person to person. For example someone who has been shaving with a razor for a very long time will take differently to electric shavers than one who has not. Hair texture also matters.    That said, I chose the foil over my existing dual-rotor philips because it does not shave a thin layer of skin as well. I tested this by applying after shave post using each shaver type to see how much it stings. The foil types burn far lesser than the rotary kind. So if you want smoother skin post your shave this is the one.    However, the Braun Series 7 also has in the middle of the two foil (domes) a splicer. The splicer does take some skin off and you notice that in the neck area where you might have put some more effort shaving. (the hard to reach areas implying more effort shaving were also the areas that stung more with the after shave)    The Series 7 offers a good close shave and gets several days of stubble off without any extra effort. The on board trimmer is very useful for a trim and to get the stubborn few strands left. The neck area takes longest otherwise you can a have a quick shave.     Where earlier the foil-only shavers were inept, this one with the combination of foil, splicers and a trimmer makes for the best foil shaver around.    Negatives - This is a loud shaver. Unlike my rotary shaver this one does not take all the cut hair inside, it does splay around, you need to shave in front of a sink. Unless its daily, where the tiny cut hairs go inside.    The Cleaner. I tried to figure out how on what basis it determines when it needs a clean. From my understanding unless it has some very advanced current state sensors the simplest way is to have a counter of how many times the shaver is switched on and off and to set cleaning levels from there. (please correct me, i am only speculating)    My experience for the above is after two full shaves and a small trim the cleaning station demanded a maximum clean. I must have switched it on and off several times during this time.     The cleaning process is noisy, as the shaver switches on and off (which by itself is loud). It also consumes quite a bit of time.    You can clean it manually, which is what you would do most of the time. I don&#x27;t see great use of the cleaning function aside the fact that I think it disinfects and smells quite ok.    Battery lasts a long time, judging from current use. I haven&#x27;t run it to dry yet as I returned it to station for cleaning a few times so it charges by default.    I would suggest get the cheapest of the 7 series models, or if you want the cleaning option get this one here. They all fundamentally work the same except for cleaning functions and some features. It does offer a close shave and is good to the skin.</li>
    <li> This is by far the best electric shaver I&#x27;ve ever used, and I&#x27;ve used almost ever brand that&#x27;s been on the market for the last 40 years. I recommend this shaver without reservation or equivocation. CGDIII, Houston, TX</li>

    <li> I bought a Braun Series 7-760 in November 2010 and when I started to shave with it I was alarmed by the fact that when it cut the whiskers from my face, the cuttings would fall out and litter the sink that I shave over. I thought \\&quot;Well, this isn&#x27;t right\\&quot; and contacted Braun about it. They assured me that this was not supposed to happen and advised me to send it to be repaired. Well, I called the two service centers in Mass. and neither one of them had ever heard of such a problem so I took advantage of the money-back guarantee and returned the shaver to Braun&#x27;s returns processing center. I purchased another shaver, same model and the SAME thing happens. I thought maybe I hadn&#x27;t set the head on the shaver correctly or something. At one point I shaved a 4-day accumulation of growth from my face and the cuttings were falling all over my hand -- felt like bugs were flying into me! Very strange. So I contacted Braun again and they asked that I please send it to a service center, which I did. I then heard back from the service center that because this shaver is not a \\&quot;closed unit,\\&quot; the clippings will indeed fall out. Apparently, the design that allows for the cleaning fluid to flow through the unit also allows the cut hair to fall out during shaving. Not sure why no other review I have read mentions this. I find this to be very aggravating -- you have to clean up all the clippings after every shave! After complaining to Braun once again they emailed me that a \\&quot;small amount\\&quot; of clippings falling out of the shaver during each shave is not unusual.     All that being said, the shaver is lighter than it looks and it does provide a very close/comfortable shave. My big complaint is that it&#x27;s so messy to use. Also, the cleaning fluid can get expensive to use when you figure out the cost for a few years. Also, I put the unit through the cleaning cycle and it was VERY loud -- I thought I had put the shaver in the base incorrectly -- it sounded like someone was cutting metal with an electric saw in my house!    For the money this unit costs, you should be able to get a close shave without having to deal with cuttings all over the sink and countertop, but I will repeat that the shave is very close.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve had the Braun 760 for about a month now. I replaced an older Series 5 which I had for several years and was happy with.  It was due for a replacement blade and foil so I decided to upgrade to the 760 and the price seemed reasonable on Amazon.  I&#x27;ve used Brauns for most of my shaving life and been satisfied. The 760 was a bit more money than the old Series 5 I had and includes the Clean and Renew system which I had never used before - more on that later.    The 760 is a truly impressive shaver. It is a noticably faster and closer shave while being more comfortable than my old one. The 760 offers two main advances over my older Series 5 which make a big difference. The main advance is the integrated blade and foil cassette rather than the older separate cutting block and foil arrangement. The integrated cassette provides a very smooth and close shave. All the marketing buzz words like triple action, pulsonic, and optifoil really do add up to an effective shaving system. The foils move separately in multiple dimensions to closely track your face&#x27;s bumps, nooks, and crannies. The integrated blade allows it to closely track the foils without burning. The shaver is also much quieter than my old one. While I thought the personalization mode was a gimmick,I have been using it on more sensitive spots on my face. Basically, it is a button which slows the shaver down, but it is effective. The other major advance is the abiltiy to rinse the shaver in water. This is important for travel. I never have to use the brush now. A rinse is quick and very effective.    I was fully prepared to dislike the Clean and Renew system as a gimmick to sell the cleaning cartridges. However, I have been very impressed with it. Simple to use and it is very thorough with the shaver coming out looking like new. No goo or films on it. I don&#x27;t use it every day and am on my second month of the first cartridge using it every few days. It is a bit noisy when it goes through the cycles, but overall seems a very good system. Looks like I&#x27;ll get two months out of a cartridge, which makes it more cost effective. I was buying cleaning sprays and fluids for my old shaver and that was a lot more work. I wouldn&#x27;t be surprised if I get roped into using it more often because it is so convenient. It&#x27;s a bit bulky, but I keep it in a vanity drawer when I&#x27;m not using it. Rinsing is quick and very effective, but the clean and renew saves those few seconds in the morning for me and provides lubrication for the cutting system.    Overall, I&#x27;m very pleased with the Braun 760. Looks to be a good value to get get the clean and renew system compared to the 720, which doesn&#x27;t have the clean and renew, and the 790 which looks to be almost identical for a lot more money in a fancier color - no one watches me shave. the Braun 760 wasn&#x27;t cheap, but hey, it&#x27;s my face and I&#x27;ve been very happy with it. If you are an electric shaver guy, I can&#x27;t imagine going wrong with this shaver.    Also, my son has the Series 3 without the clean and renew, and it doesn&#x27;t have the swivel head of the 7 series, but shares the same integrated cassette block technology and rinsability - great value for a younger shaver.</li>

Braun recommends that you set the Pulsonic strength level to high for the best shave,and they are right.  I&#x27;ve noticed that this shaver allows me to get closer to my chin beard without pulling any of the whiskers out (ouch!).  It has a much more precise feel to it.  The pop out trimmer is a little unusual, but I have gotten used to it already and it does a good job.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The 7-760 cleaning system is much better too.  It senses the level of cleaning needed and reports what level cleaning it intends to do via an indicator light, but waits until you actually push a \\&quot;GO\\&quot; button.  I really like this new feature because my 8585 had this sensing technology, but proceeded with cleaning as soon as you dropped the shaver into the cleaning system.  The 7-760 cleaner is built much more like the cleaner from the 8585 Activator, and I think it does a better job than the new style of cleaner that comes with the 3 Series.  No scum is accumulating in the cleaner, and not a single whisker is left in the shaver after it is done with a light cleaning.  If you clean the shaver ever day it appears that it never has to do a deep cleaning, because I haven&#x27;t seen one yet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Braun is skimping on the case and brush these days.  The case is the same for the 3-370, 3-390 &amp; 7-760.  The 7-760 gets a little bit bigger brush, but that&#x27;s it.  No room in the case to take along the power cord.  The cleaning systems for each model use the exact same Clean &amp; Renew refills, which is nice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, I recommend this shaver.  If you&#x27;ve tried a cheaper Braun and aren&#x27;t happy, take them up on their 60-day money back offer and get this one.  I think you&#x27;ll see a big difference.     <li> About ten years ago I put away my Norelco 885 RX tri-headed rotary and started shaving with a safety razor, shaving soap, mug, and shaving brush.  The shave was much closer and I didnt irritate my neck, which happened often with the Norelco.  Recently, I had to go on a weeklong trip and didnt want to lug my mug, razor, and brush, so I took my old Norelco.  It didnt shave as close as the safety razor, it no longer held a charge (I had to shave with it plugged in) and it irritated my neck, but it was much faster.  When I got home I looked at Consumers Reports and Amazon reviews and decided to buy a Braun series 7, the intermediate model 760 cc (whatever that means).  When I opened the package a slip of paper warned me that it would take about two weeks of daily shaves before the Braun would get as close as a rotary or a safety razor.  I decided to do my own experiment. I would  continue shaving the left side of my face, chin and neck with the Norelco and use my new Braun on the right side.  For the first week the Norelco shaved closer, but, as expected, it irritated my neck.  By the end of the second week the Braun had caught up and to my fingertips gave as close a shave as the Norelco, maybe even a little closer.  I decided to bring in independent judges, my two grandsons, ages 5 and 7.  I rubbed their tender cheeks, one side with my Norelco shave, the other with the Braun shave.  As they say in scientific jargon, they were double blinded (well sort of): neither knew which brand of razor I had applied to which side of my face and neither knew what his brother had decided.  The results were equivocal. One said there was no difference and the other said the Braun side was closer.  They refused to repeat the experiment.&lt;br /&gt; I decided to keep the Braun, mostly because it was too much trouble to return to Braun; the instructions said not to return it to Amazon.  The cleaning system adds on a few bucks a month for the cartridges and is too big and heavy to carry in anovernight case; the head has a finite lifetime according to Braun, which means replacing the cassette adds another expense.  (Ive been using the same heads on the Norelco for years with no noticeable decrease in the quality of my shave.)  When I travel, Ill take just the razor and the tiny brush to clean it manually. If Im going to be away for more than a couple of weeks Ill take the cord to keep it charged.  True, the Braun doesnt irritate my skin, but Ill tell you one thing: a safety razor with a good lather and hot water beats any electric any day.  It does take longer and occasionally cuts.  Thats the tradeoff.</li>

    <li> I have used an electric shaver for many years.  I have tried a number of brands, but was disappointed by each one.  Even the best shaver I used in the past would still miss some flat lying hairs on my neck and the blades and screen wore out quickly. Man, am I impressed.  I got a close, clean shave every time, not just the very first time.  This shaver did not miss a single hair on my neck (a problem with all shavers I used in the past).  It delivered a shave equally as close as a razor without the nicks and cuts a razor can leave.  The pivoting head makes it easy to shave areas difficult to reach and reduces the time spent shaving.  The razor did not burn my face and I could wear cologne right after shaving without my face burning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What convinced me to buy the shaver is one of its best features, the clean and renew system.  After each shave, the clean and renew system thoroughly cleans and renews the blades for the next shave.  When finished cleaning the blades, a heating element dries the blades.  In minutes it is ready for the next shave.  I was skeptical of how well it could automatically clean itself, but it works great.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You do not have to use the clean and renew system after each shave, you can skip a shave or use water to clean the blades, but I would recommend you use the clean and renew feature after every shave.  No more cleaning clipped hair from the blades and running a brush through the blades to clean it.  The clean and renew system does all the cleaning for you, and even dries the blades once the solution is finished cleaning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One other nice feature is the shaver can be used with the cord while shaving if the battery is depleted.  This is a great feature for traveling, when you might not want to take the clean and renew system with you.  My previous shavers would not work with the cord if the battery was dead.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The blades are supposed to last 18 months with this shaver.  If so, the shaver will eventually pay for itself.  The blades on my previous shaver had to be replaced every 4 months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While the initial cost of the shaver may appear prohibitive, it is well worth the money.     <li> I am using my wife&#x27;s account to write this review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I bought the Braun 760cc electric shaver, type 5693, two months ago, when my old and reliable Braun 6520 died after 15 years of constant use. That makes a difference in the morning.&lt;br /&gt;Third, vibration in the handle is almost nonexistent. With the 6520, if I had to shave a two days beard, I could end up with a numbed thumb. That is not the case anymore.&lt;br /&gt;Finally, the battery seems to hold its charge much longer, although I don&#x27;t really remember for how long I could shave with my 6520 when I first bought it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In short, I am quite pleased with this new shaver and would recommend it to a friend without hesitation. The 760cc is the third electric and Braun shaver I own.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2012-02-10&lt;br /&gt;There is a \\&quot;flaw\\&quot; in the design of the Braun cleaning system. The long hair trimmer socket will get dirty over time, if you don&#x27;t clean your shaver after each shaving, as the cleaning station does not reach it. One way to clean it, then, is to use the brush, but this tool doesn&#x27;t do a great job, since it doesn&#x27;t reach all the deeper spots in the socket. Best way to do it is to blow some air.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2012-11-05&lt;br /&gt;I lower the rating from 5 to 3 stars, because after only one year of 7 days a week use, the Braun 760cc started to make a strange noise. Sporadically at first, then every day. Still under warranty, I shipped it back last week and it turned out they had to replace the head and the electric motor (they had to, because both parts are tied together). Wow! Just after one year of normal use (I never dropped the shaver). This is no good news for the future, especially if one partfails, you need to replace both and pay for both. Service was excellent, though.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2013-10-24&lt;br /&gt;I lower the rating from 3 to 2 stars, because the base of the cleaning system now leaks like a tap and spills all the liquid over the counter. It is unusable and I am left with the hand cleaning option only. The quality of the whole system is definitively low and I should look at another brand when time comes to change my electric shaver. Very disappointed by this Braun shaver. I keep the rating at 2 because it does shave well, but the quality has really gone downhill.</li>

I haven&#x27;t spent more than 5 minutes shaving in any of my shaves so far. I don&#x27;t plan to bring the cord with me on most trips because I mostly travel for 2-3 days.    In summary, this is an excellent shaver, and for my face it&#x27;s comparable to a good wet shave system. Unfortunately the price is high which means it will take a while to recoup your investment against your wet shaving system, even with the ridiculous price of blades.  For me it&#x27;s allowed me to shave every day without slicing up my face which is significant value add, and helps with offsetting the investment. Give yourself at least a few days to try out the shaver. I&#x27;m not sure if i believe it takes 3 weeks, but my shave has improved with every day of use. If you are thinking about switching to electric this is a great choice, buying the top of the line takes the guess work out of deciding if the problem is with electric&#x27;s in general or just the cheap one that you bought.</li>

Recently, I was forced to replace my shaver after using it for at least 8 years. This was not due to any failure by the shaver, but because of a fire. Enter the Braun series 7-760cc. I am amazed on every level by this product. The most important quality in a shaver is the ability to get a clean, close shave. The Braun 760cc is unmatched,period! I have a very heavy beard and a very soft face. This razor shaves my face with ZERO RAZOR BURN! It works so well that I felt I needed to add to over 100 reviews that were already available. That&#x27;s how good this razor is. I recently spent 2 weeks in India and I used this razor every day while I was there. It does not require a voltage converter or transformer to use it abroad, nor do you need to carry the cleaning base with you. Simply take the plug, and the razor which fits nicely in the attractive case that is provided with the shaver when you buy it. All you will need is the correct adapter to plug in to whatever outlet you have available, the built-in transformer will safely provide the correct voltage to charge your shaver. Having said this, I want to add that I did not charge this razor until my 15th day in India and that was simply so it would be fully charged when I returned home. That means the Braun shaver worked for 14 days without being charged once. When I am at home I use the cleaning base every day after I shave. The next morning, the razor is clean and fully charged. I have had this razor for a couple of months now (probably 3) and I have yet to replace the cleaning fluid. The indicator on the cleaning base has let me know by a yellow light that in the near future I will need to replace the cleaning solution, and there is another indicator that will tell me when this time finally arrives. The cleaning solution is easily picked up at Walmart or other department store. To wrap this up let me just say that I believe you will be very happy with this product and the use that you get from it for many years to come.</li>

    <li> There are only three reasons to buy an electric razor: save on blades, save time from buying blades or to avoid getting cut while shaving.  Other than that blades, or manual shaving are superior--no one would argue that you can get as close as shave with an electric.  The only thing they might say is \\&quot;it is close to a blade.\\&quot;    With that said, I ordered the Braun 790.  The thing has a whole lot of items to it and things you must buy to keep it going.  Unlike the Braun of old when it actually was a German company which specialized in practicality and didn&#x27;t try to milk customers into buying unnecessary things, Proctor &amp; Gamble (the maker of Tide and Crest) bought them out and changed the game.  Now you need to have this nasty alcohol solution cleaner--which must be repurchased every thirty days--in order to use your shaver.  In the past Braun was designed to be cleaned with water and a brush.  Furthermore, you need to replace the cutting block every year and a half for about forty bucks.  So any money you might have saved by not having to buy blades is eaten up by Proctor &amp; Gamble&#x27;s desire to milk as much money as it can from you!    Within a year and a half you will have spent nearly $400 to buy and maintain this razor--which will never shave as close as a blade and takes twice as long to shave as a blade.  And unlike Panasonic which allows for shaving under water, Braun must be used dry which reduces lubrication and the closeness of the shave.  All in all a raw deal, and therefore I am returning my Braun and realize the only thing this razor will help you get rid of is a lot of your money!</li>

    <li> I have used Braun shavers for over 20 years and every few a new design actually works substantially better than a prior design.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Such is the case with this unit....But I reserve the right to change my mind after a few more months of use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Irritating:  The unit assumes the cleanliness of the shaving head apparently based on the number of uses rather than actual cleanliness.  I always dust the unit out after each shave so few, if any clippings remain, but based on the number of uses it adjusts the cleanliness rating.  Maybe this wouldn&#x27;t be an issue but the lower the rating the longer the cleaning cycle runs which exposes the cleaning fluid to more air and uses it faster.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Good:  Shaver controls allow adjustment of the speed of the cutter heads.  Also the 3 heads move independently of each other as well as the entire head itself tilts to the angle of the face.  This results in a much better shave and collects almost all of my neck hairs that tend to lay almost completely flat against my skin.  Unit charges quite quickly and can be taken on trips without the base unit.  The base unit is slightly larger than palm sized but vertically it is quite tall and removing the shaver head requires additional clearance (12\\&quot; vertical space between shelves provides good access)  So plan on a tall shelf or find a spot to place it on the countertop.  The sideburn trimmer is deployed somewhat uniquely, use care as it doesn&#x27;t appear to be as sturdy as prior designs, but it does seem more suited to the task of trimming sideburns.  While charging the unit has LED&#x27;s galore blazing a trail, but thankfully the LEDs shut off 10 minutes after cleaning or charging so they thankfully are off at bedtime.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall after a month it works well and I am pleased with the results.  Note that the 7 series and the 3/5 series units use different cutter technology so the 3 or 5 series may not deliver the same results.  Also, there are 7 series shavers that do not include the \\&quot;self cleaning\\&quot; base which may ultimately be a better option for many.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have had my Braun now for 6 months and it has served me well over the months.  (increased rating to 5 stars) It continues to deliver a close shave.  Initially I had reservations about the \\&quot;self cleaning\\&quot; feature and cost of the unit but it does deliver a good consistent shave so it&#x27;s a good investment if you dislike using a regular blade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;#1  DO NOT just stick the shaver with all the whiskers in the unit and expect it to clean well.  You will just clog the base and waste your money.&lt;br /&gt;#2 After shaving (every use) pop the cutter head off the base and tap in the sink and run water through it removing any loose hairs.  Gently shake off excess water.  replace head, and return to charger.&lt;br /&gt;#3 Every 2 or 3 days after doing this start the cleaning cycle this solution through the unit and drys it.  This is when you notice a refreshed closeness of shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some additional comments.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A The unit has some alcohol based cleaner in the cartridge (smells like rubbing alcohol with some additives.  This naturally evaporates over time, but the little daily rinse adds a few stray drops to replenish back some of the liquid that evaporated.  Ultimately, I replaced the cartridge not because it was low but after 5 months it had accumulated a good bit of shavings (even with my daily rinse).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;B The shaver does have an adjustment for how close the shave will be.  START OFF with the least aggressive setting, or you may have a bit of rash from the shave.  Mine was minor for a couple days.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;C Travel with the shaver by taking the power adapter without the cleaning base.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;D After market cartridges sold by different vendors are apparently \\&quot;gray market\\&quot; items.  The cleaning solution I bought at a national retailer has lasted just like the solution that came with the unit.</li>

    <li> I got this for my son and his impressions follow.  In short, this is the best electric shaver ever!  There is not a single feature of this product I would change; Braun hit it out the ballpark on this one.  The shaver is powerful and makes quick work of my beard, even if I haven&#x27;t shaved for a few days. In my opinion, the only thing that will shave closer is a straight edge razor; something I&#x27;m not daring enough to attempt.  I am able to shave without first using an electric pre-shave lotion on my face; another thing my Phillips could not do, as it would pull some whiskers or badly irritate my skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When the Braun is used in conjunction with an electric pre-shave lotion, the results are identical as if I had shaved with a traditional foam and multi-bladed razor.  The cleaning system is fantastic!  This is the only shaver system that uses an alcohol-based cleaning solution that leaves the shaver out-of-the-box new with a fresh lemon scent every time.  Another great feature is that the cleaning solution is self-contained, so once it is used up you can empty the container and recycle it (or just throw it away if you cannot empty the contents).  Although the cleaning solution replacements are more expensive than my old shaver, they provide much greater performance.  I purchased two replacement cleaning solutions at a local big box store for $12 and each one lasts approximately 2 months.  I do not seem to have the issue with rapid evaporation of the cleaning solution as other users have reported.  I live in a sub-tropic climate and the higher humidity probably inhibits the rapid depletion of cleaning solution others have noted.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Unlike most other shavers, this one can be charged without the cleaning base, as there is a port on the shaver itself in which to plug it.  I&#x27;m never on a trip long enough to need to recharge the shaver before I get home (I&#x27;ve used it 5 days in a row without charging and it displayed 40% charge remaining) but, it is nice to know that it is available.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Another great travel feature is the sturdy case that is included.  My old shaver came with a flimsy fabric sleeve that offered zero protection.  Braun provides a rubberized, hard plastic case that will help prevent any damage to the shaver by even the roughest of luggage handlers.  The only drawback to this product is the price; it is 2-3 times the price of competing units.     <li> I have owner this shaver for almost 4 years.  It produces excellent shaves - equivalent to or better than a manual razor.  When I first used it, I got 6-8 shaves per charge. Since I travel a lot, it sometimes get cleaned with water.&lt;br /&gt;The clean and renew system is expensive if you replace the cartridge when needed.  They do not last long - at first maybe 18 charges, the second cartridge only about 10 times. See my point?  Is Braun trying steer its customers to their more expensive 799 with it&#x27;s &amp;#34;exclusive wet/dry feature&amp;#34;?  Sounds fishy to me. So for now I will not bring it into the shower or let my wife try it on her legs in the shower. I will reply to support with my ongoing concern and post their response here as I&#x27;ve noticed there were many questions surrounding the 760&#x27;s waterproofness.</li>

    <li> I love this shaver.  I must admit that I have never used any electrics but Brauns my entire life, so I can&#x27;t compare it to the other brands.  But, this is my third Braun in 20 years, and the first two were quite good, so I stuck with them.  This one is just excellent.  Both of my previous ones gave good close shaves, but this one does just as good a job with practically no irritation at all.  I think it must be that the foil screens are spring-loaded.  When I am done shaving with this 760, my face feels so good (compared to before.  With my older Brauns, I used to have to put on aftershave to cool my skin off).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have never owned a shaver with a cleaning system before.  I really like it and I think it works pretty well.  I must reiterate someone else&#x27;s comments on how to prolong the life of the cleaning solution.  I only clean the shaver once per week in the system.  The other times, I just run the shaver under the faucet.  The morning after I use the cleaning system (about 24 hours after), I take the shaver out of the cradle, then open the cleaning system, carefully remove the cartridge, and put the plastic cover back on (make sure you don&#x27;t throw away the cover when you open it the first time).  Since it is alcohol-based, most of the reason it will get too low within a month is simply due to the solution evaporating.  You want to wait 24 hours after cleaning to do this because you want all the solution that was running through the system to dry out.  My current cartridge was opened in mid-June, and more than two months later, the light indicator is still showing that my solution level is full!  With this method, I can probably get a good 4-5 months out of one cartridge!</li>

    <li> All my life, I have been a proponent of traditional wet shaving using a multi-blade cartridge.  I would occasionally use a rotary electrical shaver for convenience, but never could get the smoothness of a traditional wet shave. So I decided to explore alternative solutions.  My requirements were:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1: Close, smooth shave.  Nothing beats a blade; but the electric razor had to come pretty darn close and satisfy my rigorous requirements of no scratch when I drag my hand against my beard.&lt;br /&gt;2: Shave around my goatee:  I needed something that would come up close to my goatee without grabbing it and painfully yanking the hairs.&lt;br /&gt;3: Decent trimmer: I need to trim my goatee, hairs in my ears and around my nostrils without pain.  Also need to periodically trim some of those obscure sideways-growing neck hairs that hide in my neck wrinkles.&lt;br /&gt;4: Quiet.  I had to be able to have a comfortable conversation or listen to TV/Radio whilst shaving.&lt;br /&gt;5: Travel-Friendly:  I travel frequently and internationally.  I needed something that was easy to pack, easy to clean, easy to recharge and wouldn&#x27;t turn on accidently in the suitcase.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I researched the web heavily, watched many youtube videos of each brand,  talked to many department store demo &amp;#34;dolly&#x27;s, conferred with countless friends and acquaintances,  and narrowed my search down to a few models that would meet most of my requirements.     <li> This is my first electric shaver. I have been a blade user my entire life, but was getting tired of having to soak and lather my face prior to every shave. Don&#x27;t push too hard. If the device feels overly hot, you are pushing it into your skin too hard.&lt;br /&gt;2). Put in the time. I will usually do 2-3 passes over my face, working my way around clockwise in zones. It takes a little longer but gives a better shave.&lt;br /&gt;3.) Angles. To get that close shave, try running the shaver across your face at different angles until you find which ones work for you. For me it is turning the blades vertical, and then running them across my neck in a horizontal fashion.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My wife cannot tell the difference between the Braun and a blade now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+ Very close shave, nearly if not as close as a blade (if done right).&lt;br /&gt;+ Comfortable to hold&lt;br /&gt;+ Pop out trimmer is of a good size and position on the device.&lt;br /&gt;+ The self cleaning base always keeps the razor clean and fresh&lt;br /&gt;+ No more shaving prep work (soak, lather, etc)</li>

    <li> I have used a Braun 5-series shaver for the last 10 years,  and I thought it was great. Replaced the batteries once.  But it finally wasn&#x27;t cutting as well despite changing heads. So I began looking around and naturally looked at Braun again. Frankly, I was put off at the cost of the newest Series 7 shavers and I was not impressed with the requirement for the cleaning and charging dock that would clutter up my sink area. But now even the new Series 5 shavers have the dock. And Braun&#x27;s website has a nice comparison tool to see what your money is buying between the lower priced 5 and higher priced 7 series. Biggest difference seems to be the newest cutting system. But would it work? Was it worth the extra cost or is it a gimmick. Well, my wife settled the issue for me by purchasing the razor at a big box store for list price, but I had her return it because of the better Amazon price. So, now the test. Is it better?  In two words, absolutely yes.  First it offers 3 closeness settings, and they do really change the behavior of the razor so you need to try them to see what works for your face. The floating head really works to keep the screen at a very good cutting angle. The razor is very easy to use at odd angles to your face. My beard has kind of an oblique grain and to get the closest shave under my neck the razor must make a unique angle, and it goes very well.  As far as cleaning, the blade cartridge is very complex especially compared to my old 5-series. While you can clean this razor by running it under water and using the included brush, it is really best cleaned as Braun designed it to be, in the docking station.  So yes, the docking station is not a gimmick, but it definitely makes the razor work better. How do I know for sure?  I took the razor on vacation cleaning it the conventional way and could see it wasn&#x27;t getting as clean as it could. One trip to the docking cleaning station and it was like new. And did I mention that the razor is very quiet? I mean VERY quiet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I should also probably say that I religiously use the Afta product line of electric pre shave and after shave.  These are creamy products rather than just liquid alcohol.  Since I&#x27;ve always used them I cannot be certain if this influences the outcome for me versus someone else.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, in summary a bit pricy, but the shave is impressively smooth (as my wife will attest to), quiet and the docking station is not a gimmick. I hope that I can get 10 years out of this one too. It seems to be build like most Braun products, very solidly. Finally, this razor was rated tops by a leading consumer publication. Now I&#x27;m always suspicious about these ratings, but this product seems to live up to the score given it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Additional note, if you use a rotary razor and try a foil razor you&#x27;ll probably never go back. Although it has been a while (my razor previous to the Braun 5 was a Norelco which replaced a disappointing Remington foil product, but that was probably 30 years ago) I have never regretted the switch to Braun foil razors.  Of course every man&#x27;s beard is different.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 12/2012 - still on the original blade cassette. Braun says to change every 18 months, but I am past that now. Keeping the razor clean is essential. The cleaning system is very good at this but you still need regular manual brushing of the beard hairs from inside every once and a while. I still highly recommend this series of razor. My shave is as close as when new and takes no longer to shave.</li>

    <li> I am very curious about the ratings of this shaver system.  I&#x27;m guessing that most of the reviews are done shortly after the shaver was received and put in service. Also, I don&#x27;t have to be staring in the mirror all the time to accomplish my morning ritual.  In the end, given the reduced efficiency of the Braun over time, the Norelco and Braun shavers end up shaving about at the same level, and perhaps the Norelco even has the nod over the long haul.</li>

    <li> I replaced a 4+ year old Braun 8985 \\&quot;Series 5 Pulsonic 360\\&quot; with the recently released (as of Fall of 2010) model 7-760cc-4. I&#x27;m unsure of Braun&#x27;s confusing numbering -- the \\&quot;dash 4\\&quot; designation that comes after the \\&quot;760cc\\&quot; is printed in such a way on the box that you really have to be looking for it to notice it. If you&#x27;re not a careful shopper, you may end up with the previous \\&quot;dash 3\\&quot; version with the white base. From the descriptions I&#x27;ve read, there&#x27;s not a whole lot of difference between the two versions -- expect the same shaving performance -- but again, Braun, why the unclear numbering schemes?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As of January 2015, I&#x27;ve been using this shaver practically daily. In that time, it&#x27;s never been \\&quot;one pass perfect,\\&quot; and actually not as smooth as previous shavers (both electric and razor), but it&#x27;s close -- and actually, good enough. What&#x27;s important to me is there are no nicks or cuts, no rash, and no mess. The battery, after all these years (and it&#x27;s constantly in the charger, unless I&#x27;m traveling), remains rock solid. I&#x27;m betting the total useful run time is shorter than when it was new, but the battery is storing enough juice that the motor runs strong. I&#x27;m not even considering a replacement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Rather than write a bunch more about the performance of this shaver, which is not much different than Braun shavers that came before it, and covered in hundreds of other reviews, I want to point out some of the differences from the previous 8985 and the other Braun shavers of that generation, for those of you considering replacement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The shaver itself is much smaller in diameter and easier / more comfortable to grip. This was easily my biggest complaint of the old Braun shavers -- the grip area was similar in cross section to a big bar of soap, and I really noticed it having switched over from a fairly slender &amp; comfortable Panasonic. The hard plastic exterior is now covered in a slightly cushy rubberized covering.  The overall ergonomics of the 760cc are imminently more hand-friendly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The old slider switch (you know -- On &gt; lock the pivoting head &gt; trimmer pop-up) has been replaced. The new power switch is a glowing on/off push button affair. On either side of the push button are silver + and - buttons to control the shavers speed in three steps. With each change in speed, the power button glows more dimly or brightly. This, I believe, is the 3-stage \\&quot;personalization mode\\&quot; referenced in the product description. A bit bogus, I believe, unless you shave at other than full speed. In fact, their user manual recommends something to the effect of, \\&quot;leave it at the &#x27;+&#x27; (full speed) position for day to day shaving\\&quot;. Regardless, it will turn on in whichever of the three settings you turn it off in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - Speaking of the pop-up trimmer, the trimmer is now disassociated with the power switch, and pops **out** from the shaver body. Its cutting surface is about half the length of the old one, i.e. very small. I&#x27;m trying to get used to it. The old trimmer took some practice to orient correctly while looking in the mirror, but in general, the shaver body itself was kept vertical. I only had to work at getting the shaver level around one axis. This new one -- jeez, it sticks out from the shaver body at a bit of at angle, and the cutting surface is arced a little like a kitchen chef&#x27;s knife, and so I&#x27;m struggling a bit to twist it three different ways to get a straight cut while looking in the mirror. Probably a bit comical to watch, and hopefully I&#x27;ll grow more accustom to it as the weeks wear on. Trimming cleanly around the ears is suddenly challenging.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The pivoting head can be locked in place with a slider switch now located on the side of the head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The shape of the shaver, in general, is slightly banana contoured. The shaving head itself is canted inward -- not the straight \\&quot;candy bar\\&quot; approach of the older generation. Nice ergonomic change, though subtle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The charge indicator is no longer just an LED -- there&#x27;s now a whole clock dial type affair on the butt end of the shaver (or the top of the shaver when it&#x27;s docked in the charging base). Moving around the dial, it shows 100/80/60/40/20% charge with a separate LED underneath each number (20% flashes red). Frankly, a bit gimmicky -- especially since it fully charges in an hour. This clock face also has an LED-lit reminder icon to replace the shaving foil &amp; blade, which ought to illuminate every 18 months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - On the topic of charging, this model uses Li-Ion battery cells vs. Nickel-Hydride in the previous version. Both have a claimed 50 minute run time, and both charged in one hour. And the old model was still running pretty strong after 4 years of continuous use. I think the real improvement here was Li-Ion provides equivalent performance in a smaller, lighter package. I don&#x27;t know whether the charge is topped off every time it is set in the base, but I&#x27;ve yet to see my battery drop into the 80% range (charge scale is graduated 100% - 80% - 60% etc.). It&#x27;s hard to be sure, since the charging LEDs go dark after 10 minutes of inactivity.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The base unit has changed a bit, but it still does the same old thing as before. Same Clean and Renew cartridge refills. Cartridges slide in with a little resistance now, almost as if they&#x27;re locking in place, but eh, what for?  The push-to-clean / push-to-unlock switch of yore has been replaced with a big round \\&quot;start\\&quot; button. This means the shaver is no longer physically latched into the base when cleaning. The graphics are revised (gone are the \\&quot;Eco,\\&quot; \\&quot;Normal\\&quot; and \\&quot;Intensive\\&quot; cleaning cycle indicators, replaced with icons of 1-drop, 2-drops and 3-drops of cleaning solution). There&#x27;s a \\&quot;check mark\\&quot; graphic that illuminates when the cleaning cycle is complete. Cleaning &amp; heated drying takes 35 to 45 minutes, depending on which cycle is (automatically) selected.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The cleaning cycle is 1/2 as quiet as the previous model. The pump that circulates the cleaning solution is now pretty close to silent -- no more whiny squeal. But when the shaver switches on it&#x27;s as loud as it was previously, which was about as loud as the whiny squeal of the circulation pump. So, like I said, half as loud. :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - An annoyance with the base unit is that it powers down after 10 minutes of inactivity. Walk away from it, and when you return, the only LED illuminated will be the one indicating the fluid level remaining in the Clean and Renew cartridge. Even the illuminated % charge indicator and the \\&quot;check mark\\&quot; LED indicating completion of the cleaning cycle go dark. Why they bothered with a \\&quot;cleaning cycle complete\\&quot; LED is beyond me if it&#x27;s only going to be lit for 10 minutes following completion of the cycle. One press of the base unit&#x27;s giant \\&quot;Start\\&quot; button will get everything glowing again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - The cord still can plug directly into the shaver for travel. The power connector is now a 90 plug that hugs the body of the base unit, no longer sticking straight out as it does on the older models, making it easier to set against the wall on a narrow bathroom shelf. The shaver still comes with a travel case, though it&#x27;s a zippered / soft shell deal now (in some ways a nice improvement, as long as my shaver doesn&#x27;t actually switch on while packed in my luggage). The cleaning brush has grown quite dainty -- thimble sized, you might say -- but, to counter that, this new model has better waterproofing so can more easily be rinsed out under the faucet. Although I never had a problem nor hesitation in water rinsing the old one when I took it on the road.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - Most importantly, the 760cc seems to shave about the same as the 8985 it replaced. And in the end, that&#x27;s what matters. Not quite as close as a razor, but good enough to get me through the day.&#x27;s now a whole clock dial type affair on the butt end of the shaver (or the top of the shaver when it&#x27;s docked in the charging base). Moving around the dial, it shows 100/80/60/40/20% charge with a separate LED underneath each number (20% flashes red). Frankly, a bit gimmicky -- especially since it fully charges in an hour. This clock face also has an LED-lit reminder icon to replace the shaving foil &amp; blade, which ought to illuminate every 18 months.     - On the topic of charging, this model uses Li-Ion battery cells vs. Nickel-Hydride in the previous version. Both have a claimed 50 minute run time, and both charged in one hour. And the old model was still running pretty strong after 4 years of continuous use. I think the real improvement here was Li-Ion provides equivalent performance in a smaller, lighter package. I don&#x27;t know whether the charge is topped off every time it is set in the base, but I&#x27;ve yet to see my battery drop into the 80% range (charge scale is graduated 100% - 80% - 60% etc.). It&#x27;s hard to be sure, since the charging LEDs go dark after 10 minutes of inactivity.      - The base unit has changed a bit, but it still does the same old thing as before. Same Clean and Renew cartridge refills. Cartridges slide in with a little resistance now, almost as if they&#x27;re locking in place, but eh, what for?  The push-to-clean / push-to-unlock switch of yore has been replaced with a big round \\&quot;start\\&quot; button. This means the shaver is no longer physically latched into the base when cleaning. The graphics are revised (gone are the \\&quot;Eco,\\&quot; \\&quot;Normal\\&quot; and \\&quot;Intensive\\&quot; cleaning cycle indicators, replaced with icons of 1-drop, 2-drops and 3-drops of cleaning solution). There&#x27;s a \\&quot;check mark\\&quot; graphic that illuminates when the cleaning cycle is complete. Cleaning &amp; heated drying takes 35 to 45 minutes, depending on which cycle is (automatically) selected.     - The cleaning cycle is 1/2 as quiet as the previous model. The pump that circulates the cleaning solution is nowpretty close to silent -- no more whiny squeal. But when the shaver switches on it&#x27;s as loud as it was previously, which was about as loud as the whiny squeal of the circulation pump. So, like I said, half as loud. :)     - An annoyance with the base unit is that it powers down after 10 minutes of inactivity. Walk away from it, and when you return, the only LED illuminated will be the one indicating the fluid level remaining in the Clean and Renew cartridge. Even the illuminated % charge indicator and the \\&quot;check mark\\&quot; LED indicating completion of the cleaning cycle go dark. Why they bothered with a \\&quot;cleaning cycle complete\\&quot; LED is beyond me if it&#x27;s only going to be lit for 10 minutes following completion of the cycle. One press of the base unit&#x27;s giant \\&quot;Start\\&quot; button will get everything glowing again.     - The cord still can plug directly into the shaver for travel. The power connector is now a 90 plug that hugs the body of the base unit, no longer sticking straight out as it does on the older models, making it easier to set against the wall on a narrow bathroom shelf. The shaver still comes with a travel case, though it&#x27;s a zippered / soft shell deal now (in some ways a nice improvement, as long as my shaver doesn&#x27;t actually switch on while packed in my luggage). The cleaning brush has grown quite dainty -- thimble sized, you might say -- but, to counter that, this new model has better waterproofing so can more easily be rinsed out under the faucet. Although I never had a problem nor hesitation in water rinsing the old one when I took it on the road.     - Most importantly, the 760cc seems to shave about the same as the 8985 it replaced. And in the end, that&#x27;s what matters. Not quite as close as a razor, but good enough to get me through the day.</li>
    <li> The 760cc is my 4th Braun shaver. Braun is the still the best electric shaver out there. I take blood thinner medication and I must use an electric shaver.     <li> Definitely not a close shave as compared to a hand held razor.&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not sure how it compares to other electric razors since my goal was to replace my hand held razor.</li>
    <li> Where has this razor been all my life. No more razor burn and ingrown hairs. The charging/cleaning base is easiest (just drop it in and push a button), but there are a couple of negatives to that approach. First, the fluid, which is an alcohol/lubricant, has a strange odor which I don&#x27;t love. Not a big deal, but that close to your nose, I could do without it. Second, the fluid is a consumable which needs to be changed about every four weeks. The stuff isn&#x27;t that cheap. I have resorted to a combination of running it under water and using the base every other shave. It&#x27;s a good compromise for me.  On the road, I like the fact that the shaver will hold its charge for at least a week, if not longer. I don&#x27;t need to drag the base or the cord around with me.     <li> I have used Braun shavers for what seems like forever. Choosing them can significantly reduce your reliance on the (more expensive) original cleaning solution, and make the total cost lower than cheaper models. I was skeptical about the \\&quot;Pulsonic\\&quot; part of the system (the \\&quot;microvibrations\\&quot; supposed to improve shaving efficiency), but the given the models that I had available to choose from, the 760 was the most logical choice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I received the shaver, I was actually surprised to find that the shaving experience and results are considerably better than my older shaver (even with a new head and full power). The water-washable feature was all I asked for: pop up the screen, run the shaver under water for a couple of seconds, and you&#x27;re done. I will not be able to go back, and it looks like I will only use the cleaner function once a month, or perhaps even less frequently(tip: if you choose to go that route, you really need to keep the cleaning solution container closed with its original cap when not in use, as it will evaporate completely after a few weeks if left open in the cleaner).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A few weeks after I got the shaver, it fell on the bathroom counter from a higher shelf, and stopped working right (making louder noises and not shaving well). Since I bought it in the US, but used it abroad, I didn&#x27;t have any documentation save for the Amazon receipt (printed from the website). The local Braun lab took it in, determined there was a broken part that needs to be replaced, and did it under warranty (it looks like they practically replaced the entire \\&quot;head\\&quot;). While it took a few days longer than I expected to get the part to the lab (holiday season and all), I was really happy with the service, and very happy with the end result. Doing a relatively big replacement under warranty with \\&quot;skimpy\\&quot; evidence and no original documentation deserves special praise in this day and age.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall positives:&lt;br /&gt;- Water washable.&lt;br /&gt;- Excellent shaving experience.&lt;br /&gt;- Excellent service.&lt;br /&gt;- Quality feel and build.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall negatives:&lt;br /&gt;- Shaving \\&quot;strength\\&quot; buttons not easily findable by touch (yes, I&#x27;m nitpicking here).&lt;br /&gt;- Higher priced than some competitors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I definitely recommend this model, or any equivalent model with the water-washable feature.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;m a first time Braun customer, and I can honestly say that I was terrified that this electric razor wouldn&#x27;t live up to my expectations. Gladly, I was wrong. Being a mixed race person, I have had trouble shaving my whole life. From irritation to razor bumps to the razor not getting all of the hairs. This product makes a damn good improvement on all of those. It is extremely comfortable to shave with, it gently massages the face and I actually look forward to shaving with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have been using it for about a month now and the manufacturer didn&#x27;t lie when they said it takes a few weeks for your face to get used to it. Those first few shaves were a little disappointing to me, but after a while I noticed shaves were getting easier and it was cutting more hair. I don&#x27;t get any irritation WHATSOEVER and I hardly get any razor bumps at all, and the only reason I get them is because I allow my beard to grow out instead of shaving more often. I went from having a moderate amount of bumps to having 2 or 3 here and there (which are easy to remedy by using Bump Patrol and/or a tweezer). Even when you let your hair grow out, you get significantly less bumps than using a razor and letting it grow out. I HIGHLY recommend this and Bump Patrol to my curly haired brothers, it will ease your pain. There isn&#x27;t any pulling, it&#x27;s just a straight cut and the 3 different personalization modes are very convenient for certain parts of the face that require less or more power.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That being said, this product does have a bit of a problem sometimes cutting flat lying hair; presumably for me because of the curliness. If I allow my hair to grow out a few days worth I have to use the trimmer to cut it low and then use the head to get it shorter. If I shaved everyday I probably wouldn&#x27;t have this problem, but I&#x27;m lazy. It works well on the neck if you shave everyday or every 2 days (I shave every 2-3 days); again if you allow it to grow you will have to use the trimmer and that can be tricky on the neck. I have a small Peanut clipper and if the hair is too long on my neck I use that if the trimmer can&#x27;t get it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t know why there are some people complaining about the noise. I had a small and cheap $25 Remington and it made 10x more noise. It was annoying in the morning and I worried about waking other people up. This is much quieter and so there isn&#x27;t an issue. The cleaning unit also isn&#x27;t exorbitantly loud and when I need a normal clean it usually runs for about 20 min. I clean it once a week and I still have a great deal of uses left in the cleaning fluid before I have to buy another pack.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The cleaning fluid smells great and like many others have talked about on here is easy to conserve by removing it when you&#x27;re not cleaning the shaver and capping it; doing this prevents it from evaporating.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all I am very satisfied with this product, my only complaint would be that if you allow a few days worth of stubble to grow out it will take a while longer to shave, and subsequently require more passes. It is well worth the price I got it for ($162) and I have now become an enthusiastic Braun customer. I can only hope that their future products will be even better.</li>
